أهلية النظر والفتوى
الاجتهاد، فكيف يستدل به علی وجوبه؟ فنقول (۱) : ما يصدر من غير الأهل ليس بإفتاء حقيقة، وإنما هو حكاية عن المجتهد أنه قائل بكذا وباعتبار هذا الملحظ تجوز حكاية قول غير الإمام، فكيف يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام
وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه؟ ونحن إنما نحكى فتواهم لا غير ، فليتأمل . وتوضيحه : أن المشايخ اطلعوا على دليل الإمام، وعرفوا من أين قال ، واطلعوا على دليل أصحابه، فيرجحون دليل أصحابه على دليله، فيفتون به ولا يظن بهم أنهم عدلوا عن قوله لجهلهم بدليله ؛ فإنا نراهم قد شحنوا كتبهم بنصب الأدلة، ثم يقولون : الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف " مثلا . وحيث لم نكن نحن أهلا للنظر في الدليل، ولم نصل إلى رتبتهم في حصول شرائط التفريع والتأصيل () ، فعلينا حكاية ما يقولونه؛ لأنهم هم أتباع المذهب الذين نصبوا أنفسهم لتقريره وتحريره (۳) باجتهادهم .
وانظر إلى ما قدمناه من قول العلامة قاسم : إن المجتهدين لم يفقدوا حتى نظروا في المختلف، ورجحوا وصححوا . . . إلى أن قال : فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به، كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم .
(۱) قوله : "فنقول " هذا من تتمة كلام الخير الرملي دفع به ما عسى أن يتوهم : لما لم يجز الإفتاء لغير أهل الاجتهاد فكيف يسوغ إصدار الفتوى لأهل زماننا؟ وتوضيح
الدفع: : أن إفتاء غير المجتهد ليس بإفتاء حقيقة، إنما هو نقل كلام المجتهد، ولا يشترط للنقل معرفة الدليل، فهو يحكى ما رجحه المشايخ ، سواء كان قول الإمام أو غيره . قلت : وعلى هذا المفتى في زماننا من اجتمع فيه أهلية نقل الفتوى وإن لم يوجد فيه أهلية الإفتاء، إلا أنه لا بد له من ضرب اجتهاد ومعرفة بأحوال الناس، وذكاء ينظر به في خصوص الوقائع، وتيقظ يتنبه به على مكر الناس واحتيالهم ؛ فهذا كله من أهلية نقل الفتوى
(۲) قوله : "التفريع والتأصيل " أى تخريج الجزئيات وتأسيس القواعد
(۳) قوله : لتقريره وتحريه " أى إثباته بالدلائل وتنقيحه
The capacity for ijtihad and fatwa: Ijtihad – so how can one use it to argue for its obligation? We say (1): What issues from someone not qualified is not fatwa in reality, but rather a narration from the mujtahid that he says such-and-such. And by this consideration, narrating the saying of someone other than the Imam is permissible. So how can we be obligated to give fatwa according to the Imam's saying when the mashayikh have given fatwa contrary to it? We only narrate their fatwa, nothing else. So let it be pondered. Its clarification: The mashayikh have examined the Imam's evidence and knew why he said it, and they examined the evidence of his associates, so they prefer the evidence of the associates over his evidence, and thus they give fatwa accordingly. And one should not think they deviated from his saying due to ignorance of his evidence; for we see they have filled their books with the establishment of evidences, then they say: 'The fatwa is according to the saying of Abu Yusuf,' for example. And since we ourselves are not qualified to examine the evidence, and have not reached their rank in fulfilling the conditions of derivation and foundation, we must narrate what they say, because they are the followers of the madhhab who have devoted themselves to its establishment and refinement (3) through their ijtihad. And look at what we have presented from the saying of Allamah Qasim: 'The mujtahids are not lost; they examined the differences, gave preponderance, and corrected... until he said: It is upon us to follow the preponderant and act upon it, just as if they had given fatwa in their lifetime.' (1) His saying: 'We say' – this is continuation of the speech of Khayr al-Ramli, by which he repelled what might be imagined: Since fatwa is not permissible for non-mujtahids, how can issuing fatwa be allowed for the people of our time? The clarification of the repelling: The fatwa of a non-mujtahid is not fatwa in reality; it is only a transmission of the mujtahid's speech, and for transmission, knowledge of the evidence is not required. So he narrates what the mashayikh have given preponderance, whether it is the saying of the Imam or someone else. I say: Thus the mufti in our time is one in whom the capacity for transmitting fatwa is present, even if he does not have the capacity for ijtihad. However, he must possess a degree of ijtihad, knowledge of people's conditions, intelligence to examine particular incidents, and vigilance to be aware of people's deceit and trickery; all this is part of the capacity for transmitting fatwa. (2) His saying: 'derivation and foundation' – meaning the extraction of particulars and the establishment of principles. (3) His saying: 'its establishment and refinement' – meaning its confirmation by proofs and its revision.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical objection to the practice of muftis in the later periods of the Hanafi school. The objection is: if only a mujtahid can issue fatwa, how can non-mujtahid scholars in later times give fatwa? The answer is that their fatwa is not an independent ijtihad but a narration (حكاية) of what the earlier mujtahids — especially the mashayikh (later Hanafi authorities) — have settled upon after weighing evidence. The passage emphasizes that the mashayikh, such as Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, were fully aware of Imam Abu Hanifa's proofs but sometimes preferred the opinion of his companions due to stronger evidence. Therefore, the mufti of today is not an absolute mujtahid but a transmitter of the madhhab's established rulings. However, he must have some degree of understanding, intelligence, and awareness of people's circumstances to correctly apply the transmitted rulings. The text also quotes Allamah Qasim to reinforce that the task is to follow the preponderant view, not to engage in fresh ijtihad.

Key Terms
حكاية (hikāyah): Narration or transmission of a mujtahid's ruling without claiming independent ijtihad.
أهلية نقل الفتوى (ahliyyah naql al-fatwā): Capacity to transmit fatwa, which does not require full ijtihad but does require some skill in understanding and applying rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the nature of a fatwa issued by a non-mujtahid?
A) It is an act of independent ijtihad requiring full qualification.
B) It is a narration or transmission of the mujtahid's ruling.
C) It is invalid if the mufti does not know the evidence.
D) It is allowed only if the mufti follows Imam Abu Hanifa exclusively.

Key Takeaway
The mufti of later times issues fatwa as a narrator of the madhhab's settled positions, not as an independent mujtahid, but he must possess the capacity to correctly apply those rulings.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti

The Muqallid Mufti Must Say 'I Do Not Know'
Rule on muqallid mufti's duty to say 'la adri'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a muqallid mufti must say 'la adri' when no textual ruling is found, and explain the evidence from the chain of the three imams.

Core Idea
The mufti who does not know must say 'I do not know' or risk forging lies against Allah.

This passage establishes a crucial adab for the muqallid mufti: when he cannot find a clear textual ruling (nass) from his school, he is not permitted to derive a ruling by his own reasoning. Instead, he must humbly say 'la adri' (I do not know). The author supports this with a chain of transmission from Imam Malik through al-Shafi‘i and Ahmad, emphasizing that ignoring this obligation strikes at the vital points of scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufti's qualification
Recognize that the mufti in question is a muqallid (follower of a madhhab) and not a mujtahid. This determines his limits.
A muqallid cannot perform ijtihad.
2
State the obligation when no text is found
The muqallid must say 'la adri' and refrain from giving a fatwa based on his own opinion.
This is the core ruling of the passage.
3
Examine the evidence
The passage cites a chain: Malik → al-Shafi‘i → Ahmad → Ibn ‘Ajlan, stating that omitting 'la adri' leads to disaster.
The chain shows the consensus of the imams.
4
Understand the underlying reason
Giving a fatwa without knowledge is forgery against Allah, as warned in the Quran.
This applies even to the Prophet, who said 'la adri' regarding some matters.

جنة العالم لا أدرى
قلت : وقوله : "وإن كان المفتى مقلّداً غير مجتهد . . . إلخ " يفيد أن المقلد المحض ليس له أن يفتى فيما لم يجد فيه نصا عن أحد. ويؤيده ما في البحر عن "التاترخانية " : " وإن اختلف المتأخرون أخذ بقول واحد، فلو لم يجد من المتأخرين يجتهد برأيه، إذا كان يعرف وجوه الفقه، ويشاور أهلة" . اهـ . فقوله : "إذا كان يعرف ... إلخ " دليل على أن من لم يعرف ذلك، بل قرأ كتاباً أو أكثر، وفهمه وصار له أهلية المراجعة والوقوف على موضع الحادثة من كتاب مشهور معتمد - إذا لم يجد تلك الحادثة في كتاب ليس له أن يفتى فيها برأيه، بل عليه أن يقول : " لا أدرى (١) ، كما قال من هو أجل منه قدراً (٢)

(١) قوله : " بل عليه أن يقول : لا أدرى روى الإمام ابن الصلاح أخبرنا الشيخ الأصيل أبو القاسم منصور بن أبي المعالي بنيسابور ، قال : أخبرنا أبو المعالي محمد ابن إسماعيل الفارسي، قال: حدثنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقي ، قال : أخبرنا أبو عبد الله الحافظ ، قال : سمعت أبا عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الصفار يقول : سمعت عبد الله بن أحمد بن حنبل يقول : سمعت أبي يقول : سمعت الشافعي يقول : سمعت مالك بن أنس يقول : سمعت محمد بن عجلان يقول : "إذا أغفل العالم لا أدرى أصيبت مقاتله". قال ابن الصلاح هذا إسناد جليل، عزيز جدا؛ لاجتماع أئمة المذاهب الثلاثة فيه، بعضهم عن بعض، وروى مالك مثل ذلك عن ابن عباس رضی الله عنهما . أدب المفتى والمستفتي: ١٠/١، ١١)

والغالب أن عدم وجدانه النص لقلة اطلاعه، أو عدم معرفته بموضع المسألة المذكورة فيه ؛ إذ قل ما تقع حادثة إلا ولها ذكر في كتب المذهب، إما بعينها أو بذكر قاعدة كلية (٣) تشملها .
(٢) قوله : كما قال من هو أجل منه قدراً " راجع : أول آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى الملحقة بآخر هذا الكتاب ؛ فإن فيه كفاية لذى دراية .
(١) قوله : " بل من أيد بالوحى صلى الله عليه وسلم قال في الدر المختار: "توقف الإمام في أربع عشرة مسألة ونقل لا أدرى عن الأئمة بل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعن جبريل أيضاً. وفي رد المحتار: قوله : (بل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعن جبريل أيضا في الكرماني " : "سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن أفضل البقاع ، فقال : لا أدرى حتى أسأل جبريل، فسأله فقال : لا أدرى حتى أسأل ربي، فقال عز وجل : خير البقاع المساجد، وخير أهلها أولهم دخولا وآخرهم . خروجاً" . وفى الحقائق : أنه تنبيه لكل مفت أن لا يستنكف من التوقف فيما لا وقوف له عليه ؛ إذ المجازفة افتراء على الله تعالى بتحريم الحلال وضده، كذا في القهستاني". وقال الغزالي في "الإحياء " : وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ما أدرى أعزير نبي أم لا؟ وما أدرى أتبع ملعون أم لا؟ وما أدرى أذو القرنين نبى أم لا؟». (الدر المختار مع رد المحتار: ٨٠٠/٣، ٨٠١) (٢) قوله : "قاعدة كلية القاعدة في اللغة الأساس، وفي اصطلاح الفقهاء : "حكم کلى ينطبق على جزئيات كثيرة من أبواب متعددة تفهم منه أحكامها" . فقوله : "من أبواب متعددة يخرج الضابط الفقهي، فهو ينبطق على الجزئيات كثيرة من باب واحد كمسائل البيوع مثلا . ثم القاعدة عند الفقهاء غيرها عند النحاة والأصوليين؛ إذ أكثر القواعد الفقهية أكثرى لا كلى ، ولا يخلو أكثرها عن مستثنيات وتقييدات يعتنى الفقهاء بذكرها، ولذلك منعوا عن الإفتاء بها .
The author of al-Bahr is not among the people of ijtihad. [Request:] The garden of the scholar is 'I do not know.' I say: His statement: 'And if the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid... etc.' indicates that a pure muqallid does not have the right to give a fatwa regarding what he has not found a text from anyone. This is supported by what is in al-Bahr from al-Tatarkhaniyya: 'If the later scholars differed, he adopts one opinion. If he does not find from the later scholars, he exerts his own opinion if he knows the aspects of fiqh and consults its people.' So his statement: 'if he knows... etc.' is proof that whoever does not know that, but rather read one or more books and understood them, and attained the ability to refer and locate the incident in a well-known reliable book—if he does not find that incident in a book, he does not have the right to give a fatwa regarding it by his own opinion, but rather he must say: 'I do not know,' as said by one greater in rank than him. "This is lawful and this is unlawful," to forge lies against Allah. Indeed, those who forge lies against Allah will not succeed. A brief enjoyment, and they will have a painful punishment. It includes in its meaning whoever deviates in his fatwa, saying about the unlawful: this is lawful, or about the lawful: this is unlawful, or the like. (Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti: 1/18, 19) (1) His statement: 'But he must say: I do not know.' Imam Ibn al-Salah narrated: al-Shaykh al-Asil Abu al-Qasim Mansur ibn Abi al-Mu'ali in Nishapur informed us, he said: Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Farisi informed us, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi narrated to us, he said: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us, he said: I heard Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Saffar say: I heard 'Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal say: I heard my father say: I heard al-Shafi'i say: I heard Malik ibn Anas say: I heard Muhammad ibn 'Ajlan say: 'When the scholar omits 'I do not know,' his vital parts are struck.' Ibn al-Salah said: This is a noble chain, extremely rare, due to the gathering of the imams of the three schools, one from another. And Malik narrated similar from Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both. (Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti: 1/10, 11) The author of al-Bahr is not among the mujtahids of the Companions and those after them, rather he is supported by revelation, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And usually, his not finding the text is due to his lack of knowledge, or his not knowing the location of the mentioned issue in it; for rarely does an incident occur except that it has a mention in the books of the school, either specifically or bymentioning a comprehensive rule that includes it. (2) His statement 'as said by one greater in rank than him'—refer to the beginning of Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi appended to the end of this book; it contains sufficiency for one of understanding. (1) His statement: 'rather he is supported by revelation, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.' It is said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'The Imam hesitated in fourteen issues, and 'I do not know' is narrated from the imams, rather from the Prophet, peace be upon him, and from Jibril as well.' And in Radd al-Muhtar: his statement: 'rather from the Prophet and from Jibril as well' is in al-Karmani: 'The Messenger of Allah was asked about the best of places, and he said: I do not know until I ask Jibril, so he asked him, and he said: I do not know until I ask my Lord, so Allah said: The best of places are the mosques, and the best of their people are the first to enter and the last to exit.' And in al-Haqa'iq: it is a reminder for every mufti not to disdain pausing on what he has no knowledge of; for overstepping is forgery against Allah by forbidding the lawful and its opposite, as in al-Qahistani. And al-Ghazali said in al-Ihya': The Prophet said: 'I do not know whether 'Uzayr is a prophet or not, and I do not know whether Tabba' is accursed or not, and I do not know whether Dhul-Qarnayn is a prophet or not.' (al-Durr al-Mukhtar with Radd al-Muhtar: 3/800-801) (2) His statement: 'comprehensive rule.' al-Qa'ida linguistically means foundation, and in the terminology of the jurists: 'a universal judgment that applies to many particulars from multiple chapters, from which their rulings are understood.' His statement 'from multiple chapters' excludes the juristic principle (dabit), which applies to many particulars from one chapter, such as issues of sales, for example. Moreover, the rule according to the jurists is different from that of grammarians and usulis; for most juristic rules are 'akthari' (prevalent) not 'kulli' (universal), and most of them are not free from exceptions and restrictions that the jurists take care to mention, and therefore they forbade giving fatwa based on them.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule regarding the conduct of a mufti who is a muqallid (follower of a madhhab) and not a mujtahid. The author, quoting from earlier works, establishes that such a mufti cannot issue a fatwa based on his own opinion when he does not find a clear textual ruling (nass) from the imams of the school. He must instead say 'La adri' (I don't know). This is supported by a narration tracing back through the imams of the three major Sunni schools (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) emphasizing the importance of admitting ignorance. The passage then clarifies that the inability to find a text is usually due to the mufti's limited knowledge or lack of awareness of where the ruling is recorded, since almost every incident has a mention in the school's books either explicitly or through a comprehensive rule (qa'ida kulliya). A comprehensive rule is defined as a universal ruling that applies to many particulars from multiple fiqh chapters, distinguishing it from a juristic principle (dabit) which is specific to one chapter. However, the passage warns that most juristic rules are not universal but prevalent, and they have exceptions, so fatwa should not be given based solely on a rule without considering its exceptions. This teaching guards against the common misunderstanding that knowing general principles is sufficient for issuing fatwas; rather, the mufti must be certain of the specific ruling.

Key Terms
لا أدرى (lā adrī): The expression a mufti must use when he does not have knowledge of a ruling from the school's texts.
مقلد (muqallid): A person who follows a madhhab without being a mujtahid; he must rely on transmitted rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a muqallid mufti do when he cannot find a textual ruling for an incident in his school's books?
A) He should perform ijtihad using his own reasoning.
B) He should apply a comprehensive rule to derive the ruling.
C) He should say 'I do not know' and refrain from giving a fatwa.
D) He should consult modern scholars and issue a fatwa based on their opinion.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti who does not find a textual ruling must say 'la adri' and cannot issue a fatwa based on his own opinion.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate

The Comprehensive Rule (Qā‘idah Kulliyyah) and Its Limits in Fatwa
Definition and warning on comprehensive rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define a comprehensive rule (qā‘idah kulliyyah), distinguish it from a juristic principle (dābit), and explain why Hanafi jurists forbade issuing fatwa based solely on such rules.

Core Idea
A comprehensive rule helps understand many cases, but fatwa cannot be based on it alone due to its exceptions.

This passage provides a precise definition of a comprehensive rule (qā‘idah kulliyyah) and distinguishes it from a juristic principle (dābit). It also warns that most juristic rules are not universal but prevalent, containing exceptions. Therefore, early Hanafi jurists forbade issuing fatwa based solely on a qā‘idah without verifying the specific ruling. This lesson unpacks that warning and its implications for the mufti.

Guided Path
1
Define the qā‘idah kulliyyah
Understand the definition: a universal judgment applying to many particulars from multiple chapters.
It is more comprehensive than a dābit.
2
Distinguish it from a dābit
A dābit applies to many particulars but from one chapter only (e.g., sales).
The phrase 'from multiple chapters' is key.
3
Recognize the limitations
Most qawaid are 'akthari' (prevalent) not 'kulli' (universal) and have exceptions (istithna'at).
Exceptions exist because of specific textual rulings.
4
Apply the consequence
Jurists forbade giving fatwa based solely on a qā‘idah because of these exceptions.
Fatwa must be based on a specific ruling or a verified case.

(١) قوله : " بل عليه أن يقول : لا أدرى روى الإمام ابن الصلاح أخبرنا الشيخ الأصيل أبو القاسم منصور بن أبي المعالي بنيسابور ، قال : أخبرنا أبو المعالي محمد ابن إسماعيل الفارسي، قال: حدثنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين البيهقي ، قال : أخبرنا أبو عبد الله الحافظ ، قال : سمعت أبا عبد الله محمد بن عبد الله الصفار يقول : سمعت عبد الله بن أحمد بن حنبل يقول : سمعت أبي يقول : سمعت الشافعي يقول : سمعت مالك بن أنس يقول : سمعت محمد بن عجلان يقول : "إذا أغفل العالم لا أدرى أصيبت مقاتله". قال ابن الصلاح هذا إسناد جليل، عزيز جدا؛ لاجتماع أئمة المذاهب الثلاثة فيه، بعضهم عن بعض، وروى مالك مثل ذلك عن ابن عباس رضی الله عنهما . أدب المفتى والمستفتي: ١٠/١، ١١)

صاحب البحر ليس من أهل الاجتهاد من مجتهدى الصحابة ومن بعدهم، بل من أيد بالوحى صلى الله تعالى عليه
وسلم) .
والغالب أن عدم وجدانه النص لقلة اطلاعه، أو عدم معرفته بموضع المسألة المذكورة فيه ؛ إذ قل ما تقع حادثة إلا ولها ذكر في كتب المذهب، إما بعينها أو بذكر قاعدة كلية (٣) تشملها .
(٢) قوله : كما قال من هو أجل منه قدراً " راجع : أول آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى الملحقة بآخر هذا الكتاب ؛ فإن فيه كفاية لذى دراية .
(١) قوله : " بل من أيد بالوحى صلى الله عليه وسلم قال في الدر المختار: "توقف الإمام في أربع عشرة مسألة ونقل لا أدرى عن الأئمة بل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعن جبريل أيضاً. وفي رد المحتار: قوله : (بل عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعن جبريل أيضا في الكرماني " : "سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن أفضل البقاع ، فقال : لا أدرى حتى أسأل جبريل، فسأله فقال : لا أدرى حتى أسأل ربي، فقال عز وجل : خير البقاع المساجد، وخير أهلها أولهم دخولا وآخرهم . خروجاً" . وفى الحقائق : أنه تنبيه لكل مفت أن لا يستنكف من التوقف فيما لا وقوف له عليه ؛ إذ المجازفة افتراء على الله تعالى بتحريم الحلال وضده، كذا في القهستاني". وقال الغزالي في "الإحياء " : وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ما أدرى أعزير نبي أم لا؟ وما أدرى أتبع ملعون أم لا؟ وما أدرى أذو القرنين نبى أم لا؟». (الدر المختار مع رد المحتار: ٨٠٠/٣، ٨٠١) (٢) قوله : "قاعدة كلية القاعدة في اللغة الأساس، وفي اصطلاح الفقهاء : "حكم کلى ينطبق على جزئيات كثيرة من أبواب متعددة تفهم منه أحكامها" . فقوله : "من أبواب متعددة يخرج الضابط الفقهي، فهو ينبطق على الجزئيات كثيرة من باب واحد كمسائل البيوع مثلا . ثم القاعدة عند الفقهاء غيرها عند النحاة والأصوليين؛ إذ أكثر القواعد الفقهية أكثرى لا كلى ، ولا يخلو أكثرها عن مستثنيات وتقييدات يعتنى الفقهاء بذكرها، ولذلك منعوا عن الإفتاء بها .
The author of al-Bahr is not among the people of ijtihad. [Request:] The garden of the scholar is 'I do not know.' I say: His statement: 'And if the mufti is a muqallid, not a mujtahid... etc.' indicates that a pure muqallid does not have the right to give a fatwa regarding what he has not found a text from anyone. This is supported by what is in al-Bahr from al-Tatarkhaniyya: 'If the later scholars differed, he adopts one opinion. If he does not find from the later scholars, he exerts his own opinion if he knows the aspects of fiqh and consults its people.' So his statement: 'if he knows... etc.' is proof that whoever does not know that, but rather read one or more books and understood them, and attained the ability to refer and locate the incident in a well-known reliable book—if he does not find that incident in a book, he does not have the right to give a fatwa regarding it by his own opinion, but rather he must say: 'I do not know,' as said by one greater in rank than him. "This is lawful and this is unlawful," to forge lies against Allah. Indeed, those who forge lies against Allah will not succeed. A brief enjoyment, and they will have a painful punishment. It includes in its meaning whoever deviates in his fatwa, saying about the unlawful: this is lawful, or about the lawful: this is unlawful, or the like. (Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti: 1/18, 19) (1) His statement: 'But he must say: I do not know.' Imam Ibn al-Salah narrated: al-Shaykh al-Asil Abu al-Qasim Mansur ibn Abi al-Mu'ali in Nishapur informed us, he said: Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Farisi informed us, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Bayhaqi narrated to us, he said: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us, he said: I heard Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Saffar say: I heard 'Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal say: I heard my father say: I heard al-Shafi'i say: I heard Malik ibn Anas say: I heard Muhammad ibn 'Ajlan say: 'When the scholar omits 'I do not know,' his vital parts are struck.' Ibn al-Salah said: This is a noble chain, extremely rare, due to the gathering of the imams of the three schools, one from another. And Malik narrated similar from Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both. (Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti: 1/10, 11) The author of al-Bahr is not among the mujtahids of the Companions and those after them, rather he is supported by revelation, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And usually, his not finding the text is due to his lack of knowledge, or his not knowing the location of the mentioned issue in it; for rarely does an incident occur except that it has a mention in the books of the school, either specifically or bymentioning a comprehensive rule that includes it. (2) His statement 'as said by one greater in rank than him'—refer to the beginning of Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi appended to the end of this book; it contains sufficiency for one of understanding. (1) His statement: 'rather he is supported by revelation, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.' It is said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'The Imam hesitated in fourteen issues, and 'I do not know' is narrated from the imams, rather from the Prophet, peace be upon him, and from Jibril as well.' And in Radd al-Muhtar: his statement: 'rather from the Prophet and from Jibril as well' is in al-Karmani: 'The Messenger of Allah was asked about the best of places, and he said: I do not know until I ask Jibril, so he asked him, and he said: I do not know until I ask my Lord, so Allah said: The best of places are the mosques, and the best of their people are the first to enter and the last to exit.' And in al-Haqa'iq: it is a reminder for every mufti not to disdain pausing on what he has no knowledge of; for overstepping is forgery against Allah by forbidding the lawful and its opposite, as in al-Qahistani. And al-Ghazali said in al-Ihya': The Prophet said: 'I do not know whether 'Uzayr is a prophet or not, and I do not know whether Tabba' is accursed or not, and I do not know whether Dhul-Qarnayn is a prophet or not.' (al-Durr al-Mukhtar with Radd al-Muhtar: 3/800-801) (2) His statement: 'comprehensive rule.' al-Qa'ida linguistically means foundation, and in the terminology of the jurists: 'a universal judgment that applies to many particulars from multiple chapters, from which their rulings are understood.' His statement 'from multiple chapters' excludes the juristic principle (dabit), which applies to many particulars from one chapter, such as issues of sales, for example. Moreover, the rule according to the jurists is different from that of grammarians and usulis; for most juristic rules are 'akthari' (prevalent) not 'kulli' (universal), and most of them are not free from exceptions and restrictions that the jurists take care to mention, and therefore they forbade giving fatwa based on them.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule regarding the conduct of a mufti who is a muqallid (follower of a madhhab) and not a mujtahid. The author, quoting from earlier works, establishes that such a mufti cannot issue a fatwa based on his own opinion when he does not find a clear textual ruling (nass) from the imams of the school. He must instead say 'La adri' (I don't know). This is supported by a narration tracing back through the imams of the three major Sunni schools (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) emphasizing the importance of admitting ignorance. The passage then clarifies that the inability to find a text is usually due to the mufti's limited knowledge or lack of awareness of where the ruling is recorded, since almost every incident has a mention in the school's books either explicitly or through a comprehensive rule (qa'ida kulliya). A comprehensive rule is defined as a universal ruling that applies to many particulars from multiple fiqh chapters, distinguishing it from a juristic principle (dabit) which is specific to one chapter. However, the passage warns that most juristic rules are not universal but prevalent, and they have exceptions, so fatwa should not be given based solely on a rule without considering its exceptions. This teaching guards against the common misunderstanding that knowing general principles is sufficient for issuing fatwas; rather, the mufti must be certain of the specific ruling.

Key Terms
قاعدة كلية (qā‘idah kulliyyah): A universal juristic rule that applies to many particulars across different fiqh chapters, from which rulings can be understood.
ضابط فقهي (dābit fiqhī): A juristic principle that applies to many particulars within a single chapter, such as sales.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Hanafi jurists forbid issuing fatwa based solely on a comprehensive rule (qā‘idah kulliyyah)?
A) Because comprehensive rules are not authentic.
B) Because most comprehensive rules have numerous exceptions.
C) Because rules are only for judges, not muftis.
D) Because they prefer to use only Quran and Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
A comprehensive rule is a useful tool for understanding but can never substitute for a specific textual ruling when issuing a fatwa.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
8 min
The Mufti's Two Essential Qualifications: Ijtihad and Knowledge of People
Stressing necessity of ijtihad and knowledge of people for muftis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two essential qualifications for a mufti beyond textual knowledge and explain why knowledge of people's conditions is critical for fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must have both ijtihad and knowledge of people's realities; rigidity on texts alone wastes rights.

The Islamic legal tradition is not a mechanical application of texts. This passage from Rasm al-Mufti drives home the point that a mufti must be more than a memoriser of rulings. He must have a degree of ijtihad—independent reasoning—and a deep understanding of the people and customs of his time. Without these, his fatwa will miss the mark and may even cause injustice. Let's walk through the arguments and examples the author provides to establish this foundational principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two requirements
The passage begins by stating that a mufti must have 'darb ijtihad' and then expands to require 'ma'rifat ahwal al-nas'. Pinpoint these two terms and their relationship: ijtihad alone is insufficient; it must be paired with contextual knowledge.
The Arabic phrase 'لا بد' (la budda) indicates necessity.
2
Understand the danger of rigidity
The text warns that 'jumuud 'ala al-zaahir' (rigidity upon the apparent) leads to wasting rights. Reflect on why a literal reading without considering circumstances can produce unjust outcomes.
This echoes the Hanafi principle of 'taghayyur al-fatwa'.
3
Examine the precedents from early Hanafi imams
The passage cites that Abu Yusuf's opinions are preferred in judicial matters because he experienced cases and knew people's conditions. Also, Imam Muhammad visited dyers to learn their transactions. These examples show that the imams themselves practiced contextual ijtihad.
Note the link between 'jarb al-waqa'i' (experiencing incidents) and sound fatwa.
4
Analyze the kharaj example
The text gives a case: if a landowner cultivates with an inferior crop while able to grow a superior one, he must pay the higher kharaj. Yet the author notes 'yalam wa la yuftha bihi' (it is known but not given as fatwa). Consider why: perhaps due to hardship or change in circumstances.
This shows that even a correct legal ruling may be withheld if it leads to harm.
5
Connect to Ibn Qayyim's principle
The extended quotation from Ibn Qayyim (based on the Hanafi tradition) elaborates that the mufti must be a 'faqih' in human nature, deception, and customs. Fatwa changes with time, place, and customs. This confirms the earlier points.
Though Ibn Qayyim is Hanbali, his view is fully endorsed here.

(۱)
فلا بد للمفتى والقاضي بل والمجتهد من معرفة أحوال الناس وقد قالوا : " ومن جهل بأهل زمانه فهو جاهل " . وقدمنا أنهم قالوا : يفتى بقول أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بالقضاء؛ لكونه جرب الوقائع ، وعرف أحوال
الناس وفى البحر" عن مناقب الإمام محمد للكردري : "كان محمد يذهب
إلى الصباغين، ويسأل عن معاملتهم، وما يديرونها فيما بينهم " . اهـ . وقالوا: "إذا زرع صاحب الأرض أرضـه مـا هـو أدنى مـع قــدرتـه على الأعلى، وجب عليه خراج الأعلى، قالوا: "وهذا يعلم ولا يفتى به ؛
(۱) قوله : "معرفة أحوال الناس " قال ابن قیم رحمه الله تعالى : "الخامسة معرفة الناس، فهذا أصل عظيم يحتاج إليه المفتى والحاكم، فإن لم يكن فقيها فيه، فقيها في الأمر والنهي ثم يطبق أحدهما على الآخر، وإلا كان ما يفسد أكثر مما يصلح، فإنه إذا لم يكن فقيها في الأمر له معرفة بالناس تصور له الظالم بصورة المظلوم وعكسه، والمحق بصورة المبطل وعكسه، وراج عليه المكر والخداع والاحتيال، وتصور له الزنديق في صورة الصديق والكاذب فى صورة الصادق، ولبس كل مبطل ثوب زور تحتها الإثم والكذب والفجور، وهو الجهله بالناس وأحوالهم وعوائدهم وعرفياتهم، لا يميز هذا من هذا ، بل ينبغى له أن يكون فقيها في معرفة مكر الناس وخداعهم واحتيالهم وعوائدهم وعرفياتهم ؛ فإن الفتوى تتغير بتغير الزمان والمكان والعوائد والأحوال، وذلك كله من دين الله كما تقدم بيانه، وبالله التوفيق".
إعلام الموقعين : ٢٠٤/٤
Section: The mufti necessarily must have a degree of ijtihad. For his rigidity upon the apparent may lead to wasting of rights. (1) So the mufti, the judge, and indeed the mujtahid must necessarily have knowledge of the conditions of people. And they said: 'Whoever is ignorant of the people of his time is ignorant.' And we have previously stated that they said: 'Fatwa is given according to the opinion of Abu Yusuf regarding matters of judiciary, because he experienced incidents and knew the conditions of people.' And in al-Bahr, from Manaqib al-Imam Muhammad by al-Kardari: 'Muhammad [al-Shaybani] used to go to the dyers and ask about their transactions and what they conduct among themselves.' End. And they said: 'If the owner of land cultivates his land with what is inferior despite his ability to cultivate with what is superior, he is obligated to pay the kharaj of the superior.' They said: 'This is known but fatwa is not given accordingly.' (1) His statement: 'Knowledge of the conditions of people.' Ibn Qayyim, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'The fifth [principle] is knowledge of people. This is a great foundation needed by the mufti and the judge. For if he is not a jurist in this, [even if he is] a jurist in the command and prohibition, then he applies one to the other, otherwise he will corrupt more than he rectifies. For if he is not a jurist in the command, having knowledge of people, the oppressor appears to him in the form of the oppressed and vice versa, the rightful as the wrongful and vice versa, and deception, trickery, and fraud will pass upon him, and the heretic appears in the form of the truthful, and the liar in the form of the honest, and every wrongdoer wears a garment of falsehood beneath which are sin, lying, and immorality. And he is ignorant of people and their conditions, customs, and 'urf. He cannot distinguish this from that. Rather, he should be a jurist in knowing people's deceptions, tricks, frauds, customs, and 'urf. For fatwa changes with changing time, place, customs, and conditions, and all of that is from the religion of Allah, as has been explained. And with Allah is success.' (I'lam al-Muwaqqi'in 4/204).
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage turns to the ethical and practical qualifications of the mufti. It states that a mufti cannot merely rely on the apparent (zahir) texts; he must possess a degree of ijtihad to apply the law correctly. Otherwise, rigidity leads to injustice. He must understand the circumstances of people, as the saying goes: 'Whoever is ignorant of his contemporaries is ignorant.' The text notes that in judicial matters, preference is given to the opinions of Abu Yusuf because he experienced real cases. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani himself would visit dyers to learn about their transactions. A nuanced example is given: if a landowner cultivates with an inferior crop despite being able to grow a superior one, he must still pay the higher kharaj, but this legal fact is known and not given as a fatwa—perhaps because it could cause hardship. The lengthy quote from Ibn Qayyim (though Hanbali) is endorsed, emphasizing that the mufti must be a 'faqih' in human nature, deception, and custom, because fatwas change with time, place, and social conditions.

Key Terms
ضرب اجتهاد (darb ijtihad): A degree or level of ijtihad, meaning the mufti must have independent reasoning ability, not just blind adherence to texts.
معرفة أحوال الناس (ma'rifat ahwal al-nas): Knowledge of people's conditions, customs, manners, and deceit.
جرب الوقائع (jarb al-waqa'i): Experiencing real incidents and cases, implying practical knowledge gained from direct encounter.
تغيير الفتوى (taghayyur al-fatwa): The change of fatwa due to changes in time, place, customs, and circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the passage say that rigidity on the apparent (jumuud 'ala al-zaahir) is problematic?
A) It leads to excessive leniency in issuing fatwas.
B) It leads to wasting of rights.
C) It contradicts the majority of the Sahaba.
D) It is forbidden by ijma.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must combine ijtihad with deep understanding of people's customs and conditions, because fatwa changes with time and place.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
intermediate
12 min
Mufti Must Exercise Ijtihad and Avoid Jumud
Mufti adab: necessity of ijtihad and avoidance of jumud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that a mufti must consider custom ('urf) and clear indications (qara'in) when issuing fatwas, and identify situations where rigid adherence (jumud) to texts leads to injustice.

Core Idea
A mufti's rigidity on texts, ignoring custom and context, causes great injustice.

This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti addresses a fundamental adab: the mufti must not be a mere transmitter of rulings. He must exercise ijtihad, considering the broader context, custom, and potential consequences. The author warns that jumud (rigid adherence) leads to oppression, as illustrated by the example of land tax where a technically correct ruling is withheld to protect against abuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core problem
The passage opens with a warning: if the mufti does not exert ijtihad, oppressors will exploit the fatwa. Recognize that the mufti's role is not mechanical but contextual.
2
Examine the example from al-'Inayah
In al-'Inayah, there is a case where land is not suitable for saffron, but if the fatwa allows taking kharaj based on the apparent rule, every oppressor would claim the land grows saffron. The fatwa is withheld to prevent injustice.
This shows that the mufti must consider the likely misuse of his fatwa.
3
Examine the example from Fath al-Qadir
Similar reasoning: the fatwa is not given because it would empower oppressors. Note the concern for 'treatment is difficult' — meaning the situation is hard to remedy.
4
Extract the general lesson
The author concludes that jumud (rigidity) on the apparent transmitted text, while ignoring custom ('urf) and clear indications (qara'in), leads to loss of rights and oppression.
The mufti must be aware of people's conditions.
5
Apply the lesson to the footnoted examples
The footnotes provide real cases: taking wealth from one who abandons congregation is known but concealed; Hanafis may follow Shafi'i rulings but not publicized; and seekers of fatwa may have hidden malicious intentions. The mufti must use ijtihad to respond wisely.
These examples show the application of the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح عقود رسم المفتی
لا بد للمفتى من ضرب اجتهاد
كى لا يتجرأ الظلمة على أخذ أموال الناس " .
قال في "العناية " : "ورد بأنه كيف يجوز الكتمان؟ ولو أخذوا كان في موضعه ؛ لكونه واجبًا. وأجيب بأنا لو أفتينا بذلك لادعى كل ظالم في أرض ليس شأنها ذلك، أنها قبل هذا كانت تزرع الزعفران مثلا، فيأخذ خراج ذلك، وهو ظلم وعدوان" . اهـ .
وكذا قال في "فتح القدير " : "قالوا : لا يفتى بهذا (۱)؛ لما فيه من تسلّط الظلمة على أموال المسلمين ؛ إذ يدعى كل ظالم أن الأرض تصلح لزراعة الزعفران ونحوه، وعلاجه صعب" . اهـ.
فقد ظهر لك أن جمود المفتى أو القاضي على ظاهر المنقول، مع ترك العرف والقرائع الواضحة، والجهل بأحوال الناس - يلزم منه تضييع حقوق كثيرة، وظلم خلق كثيرين
(۱) قوله : "لا يفتي بهذا " قلت : من هذه المسائل ما فى الدر المختار وحاشيته من أن من واظب على ترك الجماعة تكاسلا يعزر بأخذ المال عنه مدة، وهذا مما يعلم ويكتم ؛ لأن الظلمة صيادون لأخذ المال متى وقع في يدهم لا يؤخذ منهم، وربما يحدثون للإنسان ذنباً لم يفعله ؛ توصلا إلى ماله . (٥٥٦/١) ومنها : أن للحنفى تقليد الشافعى بقضاء قاضي محكّم بل إفتاء عدل كما في الدر المختار (٣ / ٣٤٦-٣٤٨) بل يصح تحكيم صاحب مذهب آخر في كل المجتهدات كما في الدر أيضًا (٣٤٠/٥) لكن هذا مما يعلم ولا يفتى به كي لا يتجاسر العوام على هدم المذهب. وكذلك قالوا : يؤجر من قام بتوزيع النائبة بالعدل وإن كان الأخذ ظلما، لكن هذا يعرف ولا يعرف حتى لا يتجرأ الظلمة في الزيادة على القدر المستحق . انظر المصدر السابق : ٣٣٦/٢ .
(۲) قوله : "ظلم خلق كثيرين " فإنا نرى الرجل يأتى مستفتياً عن حكم شرعي، ويكون مراده التوصل بذلك إلى إضرار غيره، فلو أخرجنا له فتوى عما سئل عنه ، ، نكون قد شاركنا في الإثم ؛ لأنه لم يتوصل إلى مراده الذي قصده إلا بسببنا، مثلا : إذا جاء يسأل عن أخت له في حضانة أمها، وقد انتهت مدة الحضانة، ويريد أخذها من أمها، ونعلم أنه لو أخذها من أمها لضاعت عنده، وما قصده بأخذها إلا أذية أمها، أو التوصل إلى الاستيلاء على مالها، أو ليزوجها لآخر ويتزوج بها بنته أو أخته، وأمثال ذلك، فعلى المفتى إذا رأى ذلك أن يحاول فى الجواب، ويقول له : "الإضرار لا يجوز" ونحو ذلك . رسائل ابن عابدین : ۱۳۱/۲) ومن أسباب هذا الجمود النظر إلى ظاهر العبارات والحوادث وعدم معرفة كنهها ، وقد ينشأ ذلك من عدم الفرق بين العلة والحكمة وكذلك عدم الفرق بين الشرع المنزل والشرع المؤول راجع لتشريح هذا الاصطلاح: "الرسائل المنيرية (١/ ١٤١، ١٤٢ ) للشيخ أبو هبة الله الخطيب الحسنى، و أصول الإفتاء (۲/ ۱۹۲ ، ۱۹۳) للعلامة القاضي محمد تقى العثماني حفظه الله.
Explanation of the Knots of the Mufti's Drawing. A mufti must exert ijtihad so that oppressors do not become bold in taking people's wealth. He said in al-'Inayah: 'It was objected: how can concealment be permissible? If they take it, it is in its proper place because it is obligatory. And the answer: if we give a fatwa to that effect, every oppressor would claim that land which is not suitable for that, that before this it used to be planted with saffron, for example, and takes its kharaj, which is oppression and injustice.' End. Similarly said in Fath al-Qadir: 'They said: do not give fatwa on this (1); because it gives power to oppressors over the wealth of Muslims; for every oppressor claims that the land is suitable for cultivation of saffron and the like, and its treatment is difficult.' End. So it has become clear to you that the rigidity (jumud) of the mufti or judge on the apparent transmitted text, while ignoring custom and clear indications, and ignorance of people's conditions - necessarily results in the loss of many rights, and oppression of many creatures (2). (1) His saying: 'Do not give fatwa on this' - I say: among these issues is what is in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its commentary: that one who persistently abandons the congregation out of laziness is punished by taking property from him for a period, and this is something that is known but concealed; because oppressors are hunters for taking property whenever it falls into their hands, it is not taken from them, and perhaps they invent a sin for a person that he did not commit, in order to get to his property. (556/1) Among them: that a Hanafi may follow a Shafi'i in the judgment of an arbitrating judge, or even in the fatwa of an upright person, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar (3/346-348), rather, arbitration by someone of another madhhab in all mujtahid matters is valid, as in al-Durr also (5/340), but this is something that is known and is not given as fatwa so that commoners do not become bold in destroying the madhhab. Similarly, they said: one who undertakes the distribution of the disaster with justice is rewarded, even if the taking is unjust, but this is known and is not made known so that oppressors do not become bold in increasing beyond the due amount. See same source: 2/336. (2) His saying: 'oppression of many creatures' - we see a man coming as a seeker of a legal ruling, and his intention is to use that to harm others. If we issue a fatwa about what he asked, we would have participated in the sin, because he did not achieve his intended goal except through us. For example: if he comes asking about a sister of his who is in the custody of her mother, and the custody period has ended, and he wants to take her from her mother, and we know that if he takes her from her mother she will be lost with him, and his only intention is to harm her mother, or to take her property, or to marry her to another and then marry his daughter or sister to that other, and the like. In such cases, the mufti, if he sees that, should be careful in his response and say to him: 'Harm is not permissible' and so on. (Rasa'il Ibn Abidin: 2/131) Among the causes of this rigidity is looking at the apparent expressions and incidents and not knowing their true nature, and this may arise from the failure to distinguish between 'illa and hikma, and also the failure to distinguish between revealed law and interpreted law. For elaboration of this terminology, see: al-Rasa'il al-Muniriyya (1/141-142) by Shaykh Abu Hibatallah al-Khatib al-Hasani, and Usul al-Ifta (2/192-193) by Allama Qadi Muhammad Taqi al-'Uthmani, may Allah preserve him.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the conduct (adab) of the mufti, specifically the necessity for him to exercise ijtihad and not rely solely on transmitted texts (manqul). The author begins by stating that a mufti must exert ijtihad to prevent oppressors from taking people's wealth unjustly. He then cites two sources: al-'Inayah and Fath al-Qadir, which discuss a scenario where a land that is not suitable for saffron cultivation might be claimed by an oppressor to extract high taxes. The scholars say that the fatwa should be withheld in such cases because giving it would open the door to oppression. The author then draws a general lesson: rigid adherence (jumud) by a mufti or judge to the apparent meaning of transmitted texts, while ignoring custom ('urf) and clear indications (qara'in) and being ignorant of people's conditions, leads to great injustice. The footnotes provide examples: e.g., punishing someone who neglects congregation by taking his wealth—this ruling is known but not publicized to avoid oppression. Another example is a Hanafi following a Shafi'i ruling in certain cases, but this is not given as fatwa to prevent the masses from undermining the madhhab. The second footnote warns about people who seek fatwas to harm others, and the mufti must be careful not to facilitate such harm. The passage emphasizes that the mufti must understand the context and intentions, and distinguish between 'illa (effective cause) and hikma (wisdom), and between revealed law and interpreted law.

Key Terms
جمود (jumud): Rigid adherence to the apparent transmitted text without considering custom, context, or outcomes.
ضرب اجتهاد (darb ijtihad): Exerting intellectual effort to derive rulings, especially when the transmitted text does not directly address the issue or when context requires adjustment.
قرائع (qara'i'): Clear indications or circumstantial evidence that help determine the true nature of a situation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the scholars in al-'Inayah and Fath al-Qadir advise against giving the fatwa about taking kharaj from land claimed to be suitable for saffron?
A) Because saffron cultivation is actually not profitable.
B) Because it would give oppressors a pretext to unjustly take wealth.
C) Because the land belongs to the state.
D) Because the mufti is not qualified to give fatwa on land taxes.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must combine textual knowledge with contextual awareness to prevent his fatwa from becoming an instrument of oppression.

Acting Upon Weak Opinions: Fatwa vs Personal Practice
Explains when a mufti may use weak opinions in his madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two reasons a mufti cannot give fatwa with weak opinions and distinguish between the rules for fatwa and personal practice.

Core Idea
A mufti answers for the madhhab, not himself; but his own practice may follow his ijtihad.

This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti tackles a critical issue: when can a mufti act upon a weak opinion within his madhhab? The answer depends on whether he is giving a fatwa to someone else or practicing for himself. Understanding this distinction is essential for anyone who aspires to issue fatwas, as it preserves the integrity of the madhhab while allowing scholarly freedom in personal conviction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
The passage begins by asserting that a mufti who is a mujtahid within the madhhab cannot give fatwa based on his weaker ijtihad when the madhhab founders have a stronger view. This is the default rule.
The mufti's role is to transmit the madhhab, not his personal view.
2
Understand the two reasons for prohibition
First, the collective ijtihad of the madhhab founders is stronger than the mufti's personal ijtihad. Second, the questioner is asking about the madhhab of his imam, not the mufti's personal opinion.
These reasons are explicitly given in the text.
3
Examine the supporting illustrations
The passage cites Allamah Qasim's fatwa about a waqf case and al-Qaffal's practice of distinguishing between his personal view and al-Shafi'i's madhhab. These show how scholars maintained the boundary.
Al-Qaffal's example is from the Shafi'i school, but the principle is general.
4
Grasp the permissibility for personal practice
When the mufti acts for himself, he may follow his own ijtihad even if it leads to a weak or non-madhhab opinion. Evidence is given from Khizanat al-Riwayat and the practice of Ibn al-Humam.
This is because a mujtahid must follow what his ijtihad indicates.
5
Note the exception for the partial mujtahid
Those who are mujtahid only in some issues (mujtahid fi al-ba'd) must make taqlid in areas they cannot investigate, but in matters they can, they follow their ijtihad even if it leads outside the madhhab.
This clarifies the scope of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متى يجوز العمل بالضعيف اجتهادهم أقوى ليس له أن يبنى مسائل العامة على اجتهاده الأضعف، أو لأن السائل إنما جاء يستفتيه عن مذهب الإمام الذي قلده ذلك المفتي، فعليه أن يفتى بالمذهب الذى جاء المستفتى يستفتيه عنه، ولذا ذكر العلامة قاسم في فتاواه : أنه سئل عن واقف شرط لنفسه التغيير والتبديل، فصيّر الوقف لزوجته. فأجاب : أني لم أقف على اعتبار هذا في شيء من كتب علماءنا، وليس للمفتى إلا نقل ما صح عند أهل مذهبه الذين يفتي بقولهم ؛ لأن المستفتى إنما يسأل عما ذهب إليه أئمة ذلك المذهب، لا عما ينجلي للمفتى . اهـ . وكذا نقلوا عن القفال من أئمة الشافعية : أنه كان إذا جاء أحد يستفتيه عن بيع الصبرة يقول له : تسألني عن مذهبي أو عن مذهب الشافعي ؟ وكذا نقلوا عنه أنه كان أحيانًا يقول : لو اجتهدت فأدى اجتهادي إلى مذهب أبي حنيفة، فأقول : مذهب الشافعى كذا ، ولكنى أقول بمذهب أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنه جاء ليعلم ويستفتي عن مذهب الشافعي، فلا بد أن أعرفه بأنى أفتى بغيره . اهـ . وأما في حق العمل به لنفسه: فالظاهر جوازه له، ويدل عليه قول خزانة الروايات : يجوز له أن يعمل عليها وإن كان مخالفا لمذهبه . اهـ . أى لأن المجتهد يلزمه اتباع ما أدى إليه اجتهاده، ولذا ترى المحقق ابن الهمام اختار مسائل خارجة عن المذهب، ومرةً رجح في مسألة قول الإمام مالك، بين كلامهم. ووجه المنع عن العدول عما اتفق عليه أصحابنا الثلاثة وإن كان المفعى مجتهداً في المذهب أمران : الأول : إذا علم أن اجتهاد أصحاب المذهب أقوى من اجتهاده الشخصي لا يجوز له أن يبنى ما يجيب به عامة المسلمين على اجتهاد الأضعف . الثاني : المستفتي إنما يستفتيه عن مذهب إمامه لا عن مذهبه الشخصي : لأنه يقلد إمام مذهبه لا هذا المفتى فيلزم عليه أن يفتيه بما هو راجح عند إمامه . (قوله : على اعتبار هذا أى على جواز هذا التغيير والتبديل .) وقال: هذا الذى أدين به . وقدمنا عن التحرير : أن المجتهد في بعض المسائل على القول بتجزئ الاجتهاد وهو الحق - يلزمه التقليد فيما لا يقدر عليه . أى فيما لا يقدر على الاجتهاد فيه لا في غيره (قوله : لا في غيره أى لا يلزمه التقليد فيما يقدر فيه على الاجتهاد، بل عليه أن يتبع ما أدى إليه اجتهاده وإن كان ضعيفاً أو خارجاً عن المذهب، فافهم)
When is acting upon the weak permissible? Their ijtihad is stronger; he does not have the right to build public questions on his weaker ijtihad, or because the questioner only came to ask about the madhhab of the imam which that mufti follows, so he must give fatwa according to the madhhab about which the questioner came asking. Hence, Allamah Qasim mentioned in his Fatawa that he was asked about a waqif who stipulated for himself the right to change and alter, so he turned the waqf to his wife. He answered: I have not found consideration of this in any of the books of our scholars, and the mufti has only to transmit what is established by the people of his madhhab whose statement he gives fatwa by; because the questioner only asks about what the imams of that madhhab held, not about what appears to the mufti. End. Similarly, they narrated from al-Qaffal of the Shafi'i imams: when someone came to ask him about the sale of a heap, he would say: 'Do you ask me about my madhhab or about the madhhab of al-Shafi'i?' Similarly, they narrated that he sometimes said: 'If I exercise ijtihad and my ijtihad leads to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, I say: The madhhab of al-Shafi'i is such, but I say according to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa; because he came to learn and ask about the madhhab of al-Shafi'i, so I must inform him that I give fatwa by other than it.' End. As for acting upon it for himself: the apparent is its permissibility for him, and it is indicated by the saying of Khizanat al-Riwayat: 'It is permissible for him to act upon them (the weak narrations) even if it contradicts his madhhab.' End. That is because the mujtahid must follow what his ijtihad leads him to. Hence, you see the investigator Ibn al-Humam chose issues outside the madhhab, and once he preferred in an issue the statement of Imam Malik, between their statements. And the reason for forbidding deviation from what our three companions agreed upon, even if the mufti is a mujtahid in the madhhab, are two: First: If he knows that the ijtihad of the people of the madhhab is stronger than his personal ijtihad, it is not permissible for him to base his answers to general Muslims on the weaker ijtihad. Second: The questioner only asks about the madhhab of his imam, not about his personal madhhab; because he follows the imam of his madhhab, not this mufti, so he must give him fatwa according to what is preponderant according to his imam. (His statement: 'on the consideration of this' meaning on the permissibility of this change and alteration.) And he said: 'This is what I hold as my religion.' And we presented from al-Tahrir: that the mujtahid in some issues, according to the view that ijtihad can be partial (which is correct), he must make taqlid in what he is not capable of. That is, in what he is not capable of making ijtihad, not in other than it. (His statement: 'not in other than it' meaning he is not obliged to make taqlid in what he is capable of ijtihad, rather he must follow what his ijtihad leads him to even if it is weak or outside the madhhab. So understand.)
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti addresses the mufti's relationship with weak opinions within the Hanafi madhhab. It begins by stating the general prohibition: a mufti who is a mujtahid within the madhhab cannot abandon the stronger positions of the madhhab founders (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) for his own weaker ijtihad when giving fatwa to the public. The reason is twofold: first, the collective ijtihad of the madhhab founders is stronger; second, the questioner is asking about the madhhab of his imam, not the personal view of the mufti. The author supports this with a story from the Shafi'i scholar al-Qaffal, who would distinguish between his personal view and the madhhab of al-Shafi'i when asked. However, the text then clarifies that for personal practice, the mufti may act upon weak or even non-madhhab opinions if his ijtihad leads him to conclude they are correct. Evidence is given from Khizanat al-Riwayat and the practice of Ibn al-Humam, who chose opinions outside the Hanafi madhhab. The passage then discusses the exception for a partial mujtahid: he must perform taqlid in areas where he lacks ijtihad, but in matters he can investigate, he follows his own ijtihad, even if it leads to a weak or external opinion. This balances the obligation to the madhhab in public fatwa with intellectual freedom in personal practice.

Key Terms
الضعيف (al-da'if): A ruling that is not the preponderant (rajih) view within the Hanafi madhhab; weaker than the mufta bihi position.
المجتهد في المذهب (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar within a madhhab capable of weighing different narrations and preferring some over others, but not an absolute mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a mufti forbidden from giving fatwa based on his personal weaker ijtihad when the Sahibayn have a stronger view?
A) Because his personal ijtihad is inherently invalid
B) Because the questioner is asking about the madhhab of his imam, not the mufti's personal view
C) Because the mufti has no right to ijtihad at all
D) Because weak opinions are never permissible to act upon

Key Takeaway
A mufti must distinguish between his role as a transmitter of the madhhab in fatwa and his freedom to follow his own ijtihad in personal practice.

Unreliable Books: The Case of Al-Qunyah
Evaluating the reliability of certain Hanafi books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of a Hanafi fiqh book using criteria of transmission strength and authorial creed.

Core Idea
A mufti must distinguish reliable from unreliable books; authorial creed and narration strength determine authority.

Not every book that claims to present Hanafi rulings carries the same authority. Some, like al-Qunyah, are well-known but contain weak narrations and are authored by a Mu'tazili theologian. This lesson equips you with the criteria to identify such unreliable sources, a critical skill for issuing sound fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book under discussion
Locate the name 'al-Qunyah' in the passage. Note that it is explicitly listed as an unreliable book.
Al-Qunyah is a well-known Hanafi fiqh compilation.
2
Note the two criticisms against it
The passage states two reasons: weak narrations (riwayat da'ifah) and the author being a Mu'tazili (mu'tazili). Write these down.
Both factors affect the book's credibility in the Hanafi tradition.
3
Understand the consequence (consequence of unreliability)
The book is not relied upon (la yultafat ila kutubihi). Other scholars have quoted from it, but its reputation is weak.
Even if some quotes exist, the book is considered unreliable for fatwa.
4
Extract the broader principle (broader principle)
A mufti must verify the author's theological stance (aqidah) and the strength of narrations before using a book as evidence.
This aligns with usul al-ifta: only authoritative sources are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكتب الواردة فى الشرح العقيدة، حنفى الفروع، فلذلك إذا لم يوافق كلامه كتب الفقهاء الأخرى، لا يلتفت إلى كتبه وكتبه جامعة للرطب واليابس . كذا فى الفوائد البهية. ويقول المولى بركلى وفى رأس الكتب غير المعتبرة "القنية" هذه. وقد نقل عنها بعض العلماء في كتبهم لكنها مشهورة بين العلماء بالروايات الضعيفة ومصنفه معتزلى كذا فى الكشف. وله أيضاً المجتبى " شرح القدوري، مخطوطة و "زاد الأئمة " وغير ذلك من الكتب .
The books included in the commentary on 'Aqida, Hanafi branches, therefore if his statement does not agree with the books of other jurists, his books are not relied upon, and his books contain both ripe and dry. Likewise in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya. And al-Mulla Barkali says: 'At the head of the unreliable books is this al-Qunyah.' Some scholars have quoted from it in their books, but it is well-known among scholars for weak narrations, and its author is a Mu'tazili, likewise in al-Kashf. He also has al-Mujtaba, Sharh al-Quduri, a manuscript, and Zad al-A'immah, and other books.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage discusses the status of certain books in the Hanafi tradition, specifically identifying books that are not considered reliable for issuing fatwas. The author warns against relying on 'al-Qunyah' due to its weak narrations and the Mu'tazili inclination of its author. This is a critical refinement: a mufti must know which books carry authority and which do not, even if they appear comprehensive.

Key Terms
القنية (al-Qunyah): A Hanafi fiqh book considered unreliable due to weak narrations and the author's Mu'tazili theology.
معتزلى (Mu'tazili): A theological school that the author adhered to, affecting the reliability of his fiqh transmissions.
الرطب واليابس (al-ratb wa al-yabis): Literal: 'ripe and dry'. Idiom: mixture of authentic and unreliable material, indicating lack of editorial rigor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the book 'al-Qunyah' not considered reliable according to this passage?
A) It is too short
B) Its author was a Mu'tazili and the narrations are weak
C) It was written by a Shafi'i
D) It contains only branches of fiqh

Key Takeaway
A mufti must evaluate books based on the author's creed and the strength of narrations; al-Qunyah is a classic example of an unreliable work.

The Importance of the Chapter on Fatwa Etiquette
Imam al-Nawawi's opening statement on the importance of this chapter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the importance of the chapter on fatwa etiquette and identify the early scholars who authored works on this subject.

Core Idea
The etiquette of fatwa is the foundation of responsible legal guidance.

Imam al-Nawawi opens his treatise by emphasizing the paramount importance of the chapter on fatwa etiquette. He notes that many earlier scholars authored works on this topic, and his introduction sets the stage for the detailed guidance that follows. Though al-Nawawi was a Shafi'i scholar, his work is widely used across madhhabs for its universal principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's purpose
Al-Nawawi explains why he presents this chapter early: due to the general need for it. Recognize that he wrote this treatise for the benefit of muftis and mustaftis.
2
List the scholars mentioned
The text names Abu al-Qasim al-Saymari and al-Khatib al-Baghdadi as earlier authors on the subject. Note their significance as early contributors to the field.
3
Understand the cross-madhhab relevance
Even though al-Nawawi is Shafi'i, his work is studied in Hanafi circles. Understand that the principles of fatwa etiquette transcend madhhab boundaries, and Hanafi scholars have their own similar works.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم باب آداب الفتوى والمفتى والمستفتى اعلم أن هذا الباب مهم جدا، فأحببت تقديمه؛ لعموم الحاجة إليه، وقد صنف في هذا جماعة من أصحابنا، منهم: أبو القاسم الصيمري شيخ صاحب الحاوي، ثم الخطيب أبو بكر
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Chapter on the Etiquette of Fatwa, the Mufti, and the Mustafti. Know that this chapter is very important, so I loved to present it, because of the general need for it. A group of our companions have written on this: among them Abu al-Qasim al-Saymari, the teacher of the author of al-Hawi, then al-Khatib Abu Bakr...
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Imam al-Nawawi's treatise on the etiquette of fatwa. He emphasizes the paramount importance of this chapter and mentions that several Shafi'i scholars have authored works on it, listing Abu al-Qasim al-Saymari (teacher of al-Mawardi) and al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (Abu Bakr al-Khatib). This introduction sets the stage for the detailed guidance that follows. Though al-Nawawi was a Shafi'i scholar, his work is widely used across madhhabs for its universal principles.

Key Terms
آداب الفتوى (adaab al-fatwa): The etiquette and proper conduct for issuing fatwas, including qualifications, procedures, and ethical considerations.
المفتى (al-mufti): One who gives fatwas; a qualified jurist authorized to issue legal verdicts.
المستفتى (al-mustafti): The person who asks for a fatwa; the seeker of a legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The chapter on fatwa etiquette is fundamental because of the universal need for proper guidance in issuing fatwas.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti

The Gravity of Fatwa and Its Scholarly Sources
Introducing the gravity of fatwa and its key reference works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the responsibility of the mufti and identify the key classical authorities on fatwa adab.

Core Idea
The mufti stands as a deputy of Allah — issuing fatwa is a sacred trust, not a mundane opinion.

This passage from Imam al-Nawawi's 'Adab al-Mufti' opens with a profound reminder: the mufti is not merely a legal consultant but an heir of the prophets. To underscore this, al-Nawawi introduces the foundational works of al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and Ibn al-Salah, whose writings on the etiquette of fatwa set the standard. Understanding the gravity of this role is the first step in preparing for the noble task of ifta.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Weight of Fatwa
Identify the key phrases that establish the mufti's position: he is a deputy of Allah, an heir of the prophets, and performing a communal obligation. Appreciate why this makes the task serious.
The passage quotes a hadith about refraining from fatwa, indicating caution is better than haste.
2
Meet the Foundational Authorities
Note the two scholars cited: al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and Ibn al-Salah. Understand their contributions to the field of fatwa adab.
Al-Khatib wrote 'al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih'; Ibn al-Salah wrote 'Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti'.
3
Connect to Practice
Reflect on how this reverence shapes the mufti's conduct: he must be cautious, well-grounded in knowledge, and never issue fatwa lightly.

The Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi
,
(1)
11
(2)
Al-Hafiz al-Baghdadi, then Shaykh Abu 'Amr ibn al-Salah, and nothing like him was authored, and 'al-Ahkam al-Sultaniyya' is a wonderful composition, and 'al-Iqna' fi al-Fiqh wa al-Tafsir', and 'Dala'il al-Nubuwwa', and 'Adab al-Dunya wa al-Din'. He died in Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 450 AH. His biography is in Tarikh Baghdad (12:102), and Tabaqat al-Fuqaha' al-Shirazi (110), and al-Ansab al-Sam'ani (2:444), and Wafayat al-A'yan (3:247), and Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya al-Subki (5:267), and Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya al-Isnawi (415), and al-'Ibar (3:223), and al-Lubab (3:90), and Lisan al-Mizan (4:260), and al-Nujum al-Zahira (5:64), and Mir'at al-Jinan (3:72), and Shadharat al-Dhahab (3:285).
And others.
(1) Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi: Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Thabit al-Baghdadi, Abu Bakr known as al-Khatib, one of the foremost huffaz and historians. Born in Ghuzayya (diminutive form) in 392 AH; his upbringing and death were in Baghdad. He traveled to Mecca and heard hadith in Basra, Dinawar, Kufa, and elsewhere, returned to Baghdad, and was favored by Ra'is al-Ru'asa' ibn Maslama (vizier of al-Qa'im bi-Amr Allah) and his worth was recognized. Then events occurred after which he went into seclusion to Syria and stayed for a time in Damascus, Tyre, Tripoli, and Aleppo in 462 AH. He was eloquent, knowledgeable in literature, composed poetry, and was passionate about reading and authorship. Yaqut mentioned fifty-six book titles from his works, the best of which is 'Tarikh Baghdad'. Among his books are 'al-Bukhala'', 'al-Kifaya fi 'Ulum al-Riwaya fi Mustalah al-Hadith', 'al-Fawa'id al-Muntakhaba', 'al-Jami' li-Akhlaq al-Rawi wa Adab al-Sami'', 'Taqyid al-'Ilm', 'Sharaf Ashab al-Hadith', 'al-Asma' wa al-Alqab', 'al-Rihla fi Talab al-Hadith', 'al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih', and 'al-Sabiq wa al-Lahiq fi Taba'ud ma bayn al-Rawiyayn 'an Shaykh Wahid'. He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in 463 AH. When he fell ill in his final illness, he bequeathed his books and distributed all his wealth in the paths of good and to the people of hadith. (al-A'lam lil-Zirkili 1:172, his biography in Shadharat al-Dhahab 3:311, al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya 12:101, Wafayat al-A'yan 1:111, Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya al-Isnawi 1:201, Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya al-Kubra lil-Subki 3:12).
(2) He is the Imam al-Hafiz al-Mufti al-'Allama Shaykh al-Islam, Taqi al-Din Abu 'Amr 'Uthman ibn al-Mufti Salah al-Din 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Uthman ibn Musa al-Kurdi al-Shahrazuri al-Mawsili al-Shafi'i, master of hadith sciences, and he took from the imams of the Muslims with forbearance and religion
and piety. He was a pious imam, abundant in intellect, good in demeanor, deeply versed in usul and furu',
,
extreme in seeking knowledge until he became proverbial, and he exerted himself in obedience and worship. He was born in the year 577 AH in the town of Sharkhan near Shahrazur in the region of Irbil, and he became known by the epithet 'Ibn al-Salah'. He was a shaykh from the prominent shaykhs of his town, and he was known by his lineage to his town and his madhhab; thus he is al-Shahrazuri, al-Sharkhani al-Shafi'i. Among his works: 'Aqsa al-Amal wa al-Su'al fi 'Ilm Hadith al-Rasul' printed under the title 'Muqaddimat Ibn al-Salah fi 'Ulum al-Hadith', which attained a special status among scholars; 'Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti'; 'Silat al-Nasik fi Sifat al-Manasik'; 'Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyyin' (unfinished); 'Sharh al-Waraqat fi al-Usul'; and 'Fatawa Ibn al-Salah' in tafsir, hadith, usul, and fiqh. He used to give fatwa according to the Shafi'i madhhab, but he refrained from fatwa for a period before his death out of veneration for its standing, and he used to say: 'In the town there is one who takes my place.' Imam Muhyi al-Din al-Nawawi studied under him, and al-Nawawi said about him: 'The first of my shaykhs, the imam on whose knowledge, asceticism, piety, abundance of worship, and great merit there is consensus.' Ibn Khallikan said: 'When the term 'al-Shaykh' is used absolutely among hadith scholars, he is meant.' He died in 643 AH. His biography is in Shadharat al-Dhahab (5:221), al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya (13:168), Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya al-Kubra lil-Subki (5:137), Wafayat al-A'yan (3:212), and Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya al-Isnawi (2:133).
(1) Narrated by al-Bayhaqi in 'al-Madkhal', in the chapter on refraining from giving fatwa and being cautious about it, p. 439, no. 821; also narrated by al-Khatib in al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih 3:168, and al-Darimi in the chapter on...
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage opens the discussion on the adab (etiquette) of fatwa by quoting from Imam al-Nawawi's work of the same name. The author first acknowledges the key sources he has consulted: al-Khatib al-Baghdadi and Ibn al-Salah, both Shafi'i masters who authored important works on the conduct of muftis. He then provides detailed biographical notes on these two scholars, highlighting their learning, piety, and contributions. After this preface, he turns to the substance, emphasizing the grave responsibility of issuing fatwas: the mufti is an heir of the prophets, performing a communal obligation, yet exposed to the risk of error. He cites the well-known principle that 'the mufti is the one who acts on behalf of Allah' and reports a saying of Ibn al-Munkadir that the scholar stands between Allah and His creation and must be mindful of how he enters between them. The passage serves to instill awe and caution in the student of ifta, reminding them that fatwa is not a mundane task but a sacred trust.

Key Terms
الإفتاء (al-ifta'): The act of issuing a formal legal opinion (fatwa) on a matter of Islamic law.
المفتى (al-mufti): The one who issues fatwas; a qualified jurist capable of deriving rulings from the sources.
موقع عن الله تعالى (muwaqqi' 'an Allah ta'ala): One who acts as a deputy on behalf of Allah (by conveying His ruling).
فرض الكفاية (fard kifaya): A communal obligation; if some qualified individuals fulfill it, the rest are absolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The mufti's role is a sacred trust requiring deep knowledge and extreme caution.

Adab al-Mufti — Ethics of the Mufti
beginner
6 min
The Gravity of Fatwa: The Mufti as Allah's Deputy
Opening exposition of the gravity and merit of ifta', with a biographical exemplar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the mufti is considered the deputy of Allah, state the three characteristics of fatwa (great danger, immense standing, abundant merit), and describe the example of Ibn al-Salah's caution.

Core Idea
The mufti is the deputy of Allah, inheriting the prophets, yet subject to error — fatwa is a grave trust that demands wara' and knowledge.

This lesson opens Imam al-Nawawi's 'Adab al-Fatwa' by highlighting the immense seriousness of issuing fatwas. The mufti stands between Allah and His creation, fulfilling a communal obligation, but he is exposed to error. This opening sets the tone for the entire discourse on the etiquette of ifta'. The biography of Ibn al-Salah serves as a practical example of a scholar who embodied the required qualities and eventually refrained from giving fatwa out of reverence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triple nature of fatwa
Locate in the passage that fatwa is described as being of great danger (`عظيم الخطر`), immense standing (`كبير الموقع`), and abundant merit (`كثير الفضل`). Understand that these three aspects make it both a high honor and a heavy burden.
The mufti's station is high because he is the heir of prophets, but the danger lies in the possibility of error.
2
Understand the title 'deputy of Allah'
The passage states that the mufti is 'موقع عن الله تعالى' — a deputy who conveys Allah's rulings. This means the mufti must be extremely careful, as his words represent the divine law.
This title is unique to the mufti among the scholars.
3
Recognize the communal obligation (fard kifaya)
Fatwa is a fard kifaya: if some qualified scholars fulfill it, the rest are absolved. This implies that not everyone should give fatwa; only those with proper qualifications should undertake it.
The Hanafi school emphasizes that ifta' requires a mujtahid or a muqallid with deep knowledge of the madhhab.
4
Examine the biography of Ibn al-Salah
The passage provides a biography of Ibn al-Salah, a Shafi'i scholar, as an illustration of the ideal mufti: deep knowledge (mubatih fi al-usul wa al-furu'), piety (wara'), and extreme caution (he refrained from fatwa before his death). Reflect on how his actions embody the adab of a mufti.
Ibn al-Salah was a teacher of al-Nawawi and a master of hadith and fiqh.
5
Extract the lesson on the mufti's qualifications
From the description of Ibn al-Salah and the opening statements, conclude that a mufti must possess not only knowledge but also scrupulous piety (wara') and humility. He must be aware of the gravity of his task and avoid hastiness.
This directly ties to the hadith about fatwa without certain knowledge being sinful.
